              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6466969121124770501">So after that brutal cliffhanger in book 1 I stopped everything I was doing and jumped into book 2 like it was the end of the world. I knew this would be one heck of a rollercoaster ride and boy, was I right!<br/><br/>The story starts off six months after the events of book 1. While Emma’s physical wounds have healed properly, the emotional damage left a permanent mark on her soul. In the spur of a moment, she makes the effort to reconnect with her mother, Rachel, and moves in with her, creating many prob</span>
  <span id="freeText6466969121124770501" style="display:none">So after that brutal cliffhanger in book 1 I stopped everything I was doing and jumped into book 2 like it was the end of the world. I knew this would be one heck of a rollercoaster ride and boy, was I right!<br><br>The story starts off six months after the events of book 1. While Emma’s physical wounds have healed properly, the emotional damage left a permanent mark on her soul. In the spur of a moment, she makes the effort to reconnect with her mother, Rachel, and moves in with her, creating many problems. An added complication appears in the form of Rachel’s <i>much</i> younger boyfriend Jonathan. All of this, coupled with Emma and Evan’s complex relationship, was more than enough to drive me over the edge. I cried, I sobbed, I screamed, I pulled my hair out, and I almost smashed my iPad into pieces. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378019ra/733403.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I honestly don’t even know what to say now because I’m just a blubbering mess. I’ll just do a quick breakdown of the three characters who stole the show.<br><br><u>Emma</u>: Still emotionally scarred, terrified to reveal her dark thoughts to Evan and so starts to rely on Jonathan. They’ve both experienced unspeakable cruelty at the hands of loved ones, and build up a connection on that basis. She’s confused about everything in her life, but one thing is for sure: she loves Evan deeply. He’s the only one for her. <br><br><u>Evan</u>: the most thoughtful, sweetest, and protective boyfriend ever!! It was hard at times to see his pain over the choices Emma made, and he tries so hard to do the right thing. I hated reading about his suffering because it multiplied my agony by infinity.<br><br><u>Jonathan</u>: I’m probably in the minority, but I really connected with his character. His past is not only painful, it’s dark, gritty, and raw, and it’s like a Kristen Ashley character dropped into this book. To be honest, my feelings for him were conflicted. On one hand, I despised him for the threat he presented to Emma and Evan, but…I could really see how deeply wounded he was, burned from old love and scarred by his horrific past, and I wanted him to find his HEA so badly. <br><br>By far, this book’s ending was epic and jaw-dropping. I wouldn’t call it a cliffhanger, but it <i>definitely</i> leaves room for interpretation. That last line…it gave me shivers. Anticipatory shivers. Rebecca Donovan goes big with her endings and boy, do they pack a punch! After finishing this second book, there was nothing that could stop me from moving on to the third!! Definitely my favorite out of the trilogy!<br><br>5+ Breathtaking Stars!!! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6466969121124770501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3084447733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer12786330439973215052">Barely breathing is just as raw and heartbreaking as reason to breath.<br/><br/>Emma makes a spare of the moment decision to move in with her mother and try and reconnect with her, this decision creates many problems.<br/><br/>An added complication appears in the form of her mother Rachel’s much younger boyfriend Jonathan.<br/><br/>I’m not eternally sure how to write my review for barely breathing, its as good as the first book in the breathing series, I cried , sobbed screamed and cried some more just as I did on the first </span>
  <span id="freeText12786330439973215052" style="display:none">Barely breathing is just as raw and heartbreaking as reason to breath.<br /><br />Emma makes a spare of the moment decision to move in with her mother and try and reconnect with her, this decision creates many problems.<br /><br />An added complication appears in the form of her mother Rachel’s much younger boyfriend Jonathan.<br /><br />I’m not eternally sure how to write my review for barely breathing, its as good as the first book in the breathing series, I cried , sobbed screamed and cried some more just as I did on the first one, so I’m going to do a brief breakdown on the characters who stole the story.<br /><br />Emma:<br /><br />Emma is still emotionally scarred and terrified, she’s scared to reveal her dark thoughts to Evan so she starts to reveal them to Jonathan as they both have a dark past and experienced unspeakable cruelty from there loved ones. Emma is confused about everything in her life , the only thing she is most certain of is that she is in love with Evan and he’s the only one her.<br /><br />Evan:<br /><br />Evan is thoughtful, sweet and is a very protective boyfriend, he tries so hard to do the right thing. It’s so hard at times to see his pain over the choices Emma makes, you feel his suffering throughout the book. I fell in love with Evan in the first book and stayed in love with him in the this one.<br /><br />Jonathon:<br /><br />I enjoyed Jonathan’s character, although I had hatred for him over his threat to Emma and Evan. I still liked his character and could feel how deeply wounded he was. Burned from an old love and scarred by a horrific past, I really wanted a happily ever after for him, his past is dark,gritty and raw.<br /><br />After finishing the second book there was nothing stopping me from reading the third. The end of the book gave me shiver, anticipated shivers.<br /><br />The ending was epic and jaw dropping that I just couldn’t believe it.<br /><br />The breathing series is one of my top favourite series, its something I could always go back to and read again and again.<br /><br />MY RATING⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=sad">sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=liked-the-characters-some-or-all">liked-the-characters-some-or-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=cliffhangers">cliffhangers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559118644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4715416845016363377"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>This is probably the most depressing book, i have ever read in my life. When you read this, it's like you can : <i>
  <u>feel</u>
</i> the pain, and all the sadness, all those emotions are just pouring out of the pages. <br/><br/>This is how I pictured the main protagonist, Emma<br/><img src='https://www.goodreads.com/image%20<a%20href=' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413090i/812944._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo 65efaeac-5412-4d60-b607-1a349b4ca989_zps25968d33.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>" <br/>And this is how i kinda pictured Ethan, delete the tiny beard though.<br/> <img src='https://www.goodreads.com/image%20<a%20href=' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413090i/812945.jpg' alt=' photo 24da2dc9-6677-4291-a768-9440dd3e832f_zps5087586c.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>" <br/><br/>Barely Breathing is the second book in the heartbreaking Breathing trilogy, by Rebecca Donovan. May i just say, this is absolutely <i>MASSIVE</i>, it's the biggest book </span>
  <span id="freeText4715416845016363377" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br>This is probably the most depressing book, i have ever read in my life. When you read this, it's like you can : <i>
  <u>feel</u>
</i> the pain, and all the sadness, all those emotions are just pouring out of the pages. <br><br>This is how I pictured the main protagonist, Emma<br><img src="https://www.goodreads.com/image%20&lt;a%20href=" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413090i/812944._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 65efaeac-5412-4d60-b607-1a349b4ca989_zps25968d33.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">" <br>And this is how i kinda pictured Ethan, delete the tiny beard though.<br> <img src="https://www.goodreads.com/image%20&lt;a%20href=" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413090i/812945.jpg" alt=" photo 24da2dc9-6677-4291-a768-9440dd3e832f_zps5087586c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">" <br><br>Barely Breathing is the second book in the heartbreaking Breathing trilogy, by Rebecca Donovan. May i just say, this is absolutely <i>MASSIVE</i>, it's the biggest book i ever read, it has nearly 600 pages! But i actually manged to get through it fairly quickly, only took me about 3 days. It follows this 17 year old girl, named Emma, and it's basically about what she has suffered at the hands of her 'family', and how she is dealing with it. To sum it up, in the simple but really bad way, it's about her tragic life, and what she is going through.<br><br>To those of you who haven't read book one, it has first love in it, drama, romance, friendship stuff, and it has some serious abuse. If you're interested then i highly suggest you check it out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11561469.Reason_to_Breathe__Breathing___1_" title="Reason to Breathe (Breathing, #1) by Rebecca Donovan" rel="nofollow noopener">Reason to Breathe</a>, and find out more in deeper detail.<br><br>It starts a couple of months from where we left of in book one, i wasn't very happy about that, but now come to think of it, i think the author did the right thing. I couldn't really get into it, it was very boring at first. But after some 100 pages, it got better and better throughout the book, thanks goodness for that!<br><img src="https://www.goodreads.com/image%20&lt;a%20href=" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img alt="Happy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/72927.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>" <br><br>To be honest, i wouldn't be surprised to find out if someone hated this book or the previous one. They are definitely not for readers who love lot's of action and excitement, and especially happy books. So if you are one of those readers, run away from this book as far and as fast as you can.<br><br>I think what's the best thing about this trilogy, are the characters. It's so hard not to feel compassion towards at least one of them. And when you fall for one of the character, you will most likely fall for the others too. I cared about Emma and Ethan <i> very</i> deeply, i obviously had to know what's going to happen to them, so i just kept on reading. Even though Emma is the most depressing main character, she is still funny and so lovable. Her life is so tragic it's almost unreal. One bad thing after the other, i feel so sorry for her.<br><br><b> <blockquote>“I breathed for you... I begged for you to breathe with every breath I gave to you. I kept pleading for you to breathe over and over again. And then… then you did. ~ Evan” </blockquote></b> <br><br>I was very happy, as there were many romantic and heart-melting scenes between Emma and Ethan. I actually did my happy dance, because they were still together, and they even got <u>closer</u> too! <br><br><img src="https://www.goodreads.com/image%20&lt;a%20href=" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img alt="Girl Happy Dance" width="135" height="177" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377602ra/732952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">" <br><br>Now comes the dreadful moment- <b>The ending</b>. Rebecca has made it a habit now, of ending her well going books with cliffhangers, and making her readers want to throw the book out the window. She always ends them in a very sad and crushing way. I despise her for it! I was so frustrated at the end!<br><br><a href="http://s1293.beta.photobucket.com/user/booksandpoems/media/hurtmyfeelinganimation_zps433759a1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a> <br><br><b><blockquote>I knew how much Evan loved me. And I knew I didn't deserve it. But I also knew he was the only one I loved. The only one I would ever love.” </blockquote> </b><br><br>Overall, Barely breathing was an extremely well written and thought provoking read. I couldn't stop reading it, and even though there was not much action, i couldn't help but jump from the excitement sometimes. Highly recommend you picking up book 1, if you haven't already, before reading book 2. I can't wait to see what happens next, and what Rebecca has in stock for us. If book 3 won't have a happy ending, then i am never gonna read anything by this author again, and i will even contact her about how selfish she is by not giving Emma the 'happily ever after' with Ethan she really deserves.<br> </span>

<div id="review_277487511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277487511" />
    <a title="Morgan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5637577-morgan"><img alt="Morgan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373569756p2/5637577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277487511?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/5637577-morgan">Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5637577-morgan?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5637577-morgan?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277487511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13323250065541356187"><a href='http://www.readingeatinganddreaming.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>CLICK HERE TO READ MORE REVIEWS AT READING, EATING AND DREAMING I WAS BLAIR WALDORF</a><br/><br/>WOW! That was totally, one hundred percent not what I expected. I am in shock right now. I, flat-out, did not see that coming!<br/><br/>First off, I loved Reason to Breathe, the first novel in The Breathing Series. It was an intense, explosive story. While reading Reason to Breathe, I fell head over heels for Emma and Evan. Watching them fall in love helped balance out the dark, heavy, emotional side of the story that was c</span>
  <span id="freeText13323250065541356187" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingeatinganddreaming.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">CLICK HERE TO READ MORE REVIEWS AT READING, EATING AND DREAMING I WAS BLAIR WALDORF</a><br /><br />WOW! That was totally, one hundred percent not what I expected. I am in shock right now. I, flat-out, did not see that coming!<br /><br />First off, I loved Reason to Breathe, the first novel in The Breathing Series. It was an intense, explosive story. While reading Reason to Breathe, I fell head over heels for Emma and Evan. Watching them fall in love helped balance out the dark, heavy, emotional side of the story that was centered around abuse. Emma and Evan gave me a reason to smile and a reason to hope. My hope for a happily ever after, however, was shattered when Ms. Donovan ended Reason to Breathe with a gut-clenching cliffhanger.<br /><br />Shortly after completing Reason to Breathe, my hope was restored when I discovered that Ms. Donovan was in the process of writing a sequel to Reason to Breathe, titled Barely Breathing. I honestly thought that Barely Breathing was the last novel in this series. It's not. I really expected Barely Breathing to be the lighter, happier conclusion to the crazy, intense story that began this series. It wasn't. I basically assumed that Barely Breathing was going to be a really sweet story where the boy saves the girl and then they ride off in the sunset together! Not even freaking close.<br /><br />Honestly, I don't really know exactly how I feel about this novel. I had an extremely hard time assigning a STAR rating to this novel because I liked it, but at the same time, I didn't like it. There are a lot of positive things that I can say about this novel. Barely Breathing is a wonderfully written, intense novel that will keep readers on the edge of their seat. This novel is the complete opposite of generic; it's a risky story that touches on real issues that young adults face. The storyline is original and completely unpredictable. It's a good story, but it's not the story I wanted.<br /><br />I really started to really dislike Emma in this novel. Ya know the girl in the scary movie who keeps running up the stairs? That's Emma. I don't think she made ONE good decision in this entire novel. SERIOUSLY. I don't think Emma made one good decision in this entire freaking novel, and all of her poor decision, kept me from the ending that I wanted. So to be honest, I am really mad at Emma right now!<br /><br />The part of me that was looking for closure and immediate gratification was extremely disappointed with this novel. Barely Breathing leaves off with another dramatic cliffhanger. It's not quite as dramatic as Reason to Breathe, but it's dramatic, nonetheless. Fortunately, Rebecca Donovan is currently working on the third and final novel in The Breathing Series, Out of Breath. Unfortunately, I have to wait even longer now for my closure. <br /><br />I gave Barely Breathing (The Breathing Series #2) by Rebecca Donovan 4 STARS (3.5 STARS). I'm still torn about this novel, but I'm really looking forward to the next novel in the series. I know that doesn't really make a lot sense, but this novel has me all twisted up! I ended up giving this novel 4 STARS instead of 3 STARS because it's the type of story that makes an impact and leaves an impression. I won't forget this story anytime soon.<br /><br />-XOXO<br /><br /><a href="http://www.readingeatinganddreaming.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">READING, EATING AND DREAMING</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1241829774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4439091792976773999"><i>I can't decide between 3 stars or 4. So it's 3.5.<br/>This book was actually really frustrating! Every character annoyed me at one point in the book. Some more than once.<br/><br/>Again I wished for a duo POV but it didn't happen. I just find the one sided story from Emma like we only have half the story. Like when Evan left to California or whatever again because him and Emma were going through some things I'd love to be in his head at that moment. To see and feel what he is. Just assuming his side from Emma'</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4439091792976773999" style="display:none"><i>I can't decide between 3 stars or 4. So it's 3.5.<br />This book was actually really frustrating! Every character annoyed me at one point in the book. Some more than once.<br /><br />Again I wished for a duo POV but it didn't happen. I just find the one sided story from Emma like we only have half the story. Like when Evan left to California or whatever again because him and Emma were going through some things I'd love to be in his head at that moment. To see and feel what he is. Just assuming his side from Emma's POV isn't enough for me!<br /><br /><u>Emma's annoying-ness :</u> Oh where do I begin!? Maybe with how stupid she was for always spending time with Jonathan and turning to Jonathan for EVERYTHING instead of Evan. Now I like Jonathan and I get why he'd think he loves Emma because they understand each others darkness, the part of themselves they don't want anyone to know about. And I get that Emma found him easier to confide in for fear of tainting Evan or that Evan wouldn't understand. BUT FOR GOD SAKE EVAN HAS BEEN THERE FOR HER TIME AND TIME AGAIN! He loves Emma with all her darkness and past and wants to help. He was f*cking there in the house and saw her lifeless beat up body. He's seen her at her worst and IS STILL THERE! She didn't even try to tell him about her nightmares or let him in her head. And then the end happened! She F*CKING LEFT EVAN ON HIS BIRTHDAY!!! Total b*tch. Urrrrgghhhh.<br /><u>Evan's annoying-ness :</u> Him keeping Analise as a friend when he definitely knows she really likes him. Oh I hated Analise so much! I was like Sara and just wanting to slap her! But Emma didn't put her in place. Neither did Evan until Emma finally confronted him about her and her damn annoying clingy-ness. That was so un-Evan like for me. I would think Evan would set her straight. Tell her "I have a beautiful girlfriend who I love and will always love so back the f*ck off b*tch"....or something along those lines hahaha. But how he just let it go on and pretty much added fuel to the fire with him driving her everywhere and taking her parties to 'make her feel comfortable as the new girl' blahblahblah. It would take an total idiot not to notice her obsessive clingy behavior yet it went on for a while. And I was gritting my teeth everytime she'd be mentioned.<br /><u>Sara's annoying-ness : </u>How she acted like a total b*tch at the beginning. Being jealous of Emma and all. Like it as uncalled for but I understood it but still...this is Emma's first love and first pretty much everything and Sara is more experienced with everything...she really turned into a huge b*tch but thank god Jared came back.<br /><u> Jonathan's annoying-ness :</u> Now I knew the only reason he was staying with Emma's Mum was because of Emma. I felt their connection. And I will admit that at a point I wuldn't have minded Emma choosing him over Evan but then..Evan is Evan and I love him more. Love him more for Emma. But how he came in at the end and ruined everything on Evan's birthday f*cking sucked. Couldn't he have done this the next damn day!? Uggghh.<br />Emma's Mum is a colossal f*ck up. I admire Emma's persistence in trying with her but some people are damaged beyond repair.<br />Yeah this book was a whole lot of emotions.<br />I just feel sorry for Evan.<br />Next book! </i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BWDc3lJig96m9yIntW9LnwL3S0LfNsOVuDsespL67ih/u/WFEAur1Mbo/e/OX3opPAf8aPaiM6KHvvq+y0jP6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('orv48rx+epbXRmVhBz5ZXxmuPutzbqV+ap3j6LfBfjTYYNGp/hdSnLdZuql8DmjpJ16JwVr6VUlVGAfk7nNf9w==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText1371988376920120434" style="display:none">Optimism seeps from every pore of my body. I truly believe that what's supposed to happen... will! In that regard, I don't know how to give up; it's not part of my biological make up.<br /><br />I'm a passionate (and some would say, overly enthusiastic) person. I learn by doing (and have been burned more times that I'd like to admit), but I will always throw my entire self into whatever I do - fail or succeed. <br /><br />I think this is evident when I write, leaving nothing behind and spilling it all out on the pages. I give it all to my readers - love it or hate it. <br /><br />The path I'm on is very often my own, veering off the beaten path at the sight of something more interesting or captivating, getting caught in the vines and thorns in order to experience the beauty and intrigue others often pass by. And I always meet the most interesting people along the way...</span>
